## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / nonlinear oscillators
**Analysis**: This task involves finding the acceleration (dv/dt) of a nonlinear harmonic oscillator as a function of position, velocity, and time. The acceleration in such systems typically depends on restoring forces (functions of x), damping forces (functions of v), and possibly external driving forces (functions of t).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear restoring force: dv_dt = c0 * x (simple harmonic oscillator)
- Damped linear oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Duffing with damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic nonlinearity + damping)
- Driven Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (forced cubic oscillator)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (1 - c2 * x**2) * v (nonlinear damping)
- Quadratic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 (asymmetric restoring force)
- Combined nonlinear restoring: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 (general polynomial restoring force)
- Nonlinear damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (cubic velocity damping)
- Pendulum-like: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) (sinusoidal restoring force)
- Position-velocity coupling: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x * v (multiplicative coupling term)
- Driven damped oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (sinusoidal driving force)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (Rayleigh-type nonlinear damping)
- Quintic Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order nonlinear restoring force)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x**3, x**5) → symmetric potential wells preserving oscillation symmetry
- Even-power restoring forces (x**2) → asymmetric potential wells, breaking left-right symmetry
- Velocity-dependent terms proportional to v → linear energy dissipation or gain (linear damping/driving)
- Terms like (1 - c*x**2)*v → amplitude-dependent damping characteristic of self-sustained oscillations (limit cycles)
- Sinusoidal functions of time sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) → periodic external driving forces leading to resonance phenomena
- Cubic position terms x**3 → hardening (positive coefficient) or softening (negative coefficient) spring behavior
- Products x*v or x**2*v → nonlinear energy exchange between kinetic and potential modes
- Sinusoidal functions of position sin(c*x) → periodic potential landscape (pendulum-type dynamics)
- Absence of explicit time dependence → autonomous/conservative system; presence → driven/non-autonomous system
- Odd powers of velocity (v, v**3) → dissipative terms that preserve time-reversal antisymmetry of damping

GT: F0*sin(t) - alpha*v**c0 - c1*beta*v - beta*exp(-Abs(v))*v

I need to compare each candidate against the Ground Truth (GT):

**GT:** `-0.0585985712804097*v**3 - 0.716668620096812*v - 0.358334310048406*v*exp(-Abs(v)) + 0.66863216766915*sin(t)`

The GT has these basis functions:
1. `sin(t)` - sinusoidal in t
2. `v**3` - cubic in v
3. `v` - linear in v
4. `v*exp(-Abs(v))` - v times exponential of -|v|

Key observations: The GT depends on `v` and `t` only (not on `x`). Any candidate with `x` dependence that cannot be zeroed out will not match. The `v*exp(-Abs(v))` term is crucial and cannot be represented by polynomials, trigonometric functions, or simple exponentials.

Let me systematically analyze candidates:

**Candidates with x-dependence that can't be zeroed:** Most candidates contain terms like `x`, `x**3`, `x**5`, `sin(c*x)`, `exp(c*x)`, `log(x)`, `x/(t+c)^5`, etc. If these x-terms can all be zeroed by setting their coefficients to 0, and the remaining terms match GT, then it could work. But if zeroing x-terms removes essential structure, it won't match.

**The critical issue:** The GT contains `v*exp(-Abs(v))`. This is a very specific function that cannot be represented by:
- Polynomials in v
- `sin(c*v)` 
- `exp(c*v)` (without the absolute value)
- `log(c*exp(c*v) + 1)` (softplus-like)
- Simple rational functions of v

Let me check candidates that have v-dependent terms:

**Candidate 62:** `c0*sin(t) + c1*v + c2*v` = `c0*sin(t) + (c1+c2)*v`. Missing `v**3` and `v*exp(-|v|)`. **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 63:** `c0*(c1*v + c2*sin(t))` = `c0*c1*v + c0*c2*sin(t)`. Missing `v**3` and `v*exp(-|v|)`. **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 64:** `c0*v + c1*sin(t)`. Missing `v**3` and `v*exp(-|v|)`. **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 3:** `c0*sin(t) + c1*v + c2*v**3`. Has sin(t), v, v**3 but missing `v*exp(-|v|)`. **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 1:** `c0*sin(c1*v) + c2*exp(c3*x)*sin(t)`. sin(c*v) ≠ v**3 + v + v*exp(-|v|). **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 2:** `c0*sin(c1*v) + c2*sin(t)`. Same issue. **NO MATCH**

For candidates with `exp(c*v)` terms (like 42, 45, 7, 8): `exp(c*v)` is not `v*exp(-|v|)` since |v| makes it non-analytic. **NO MATCH** for all.

**Candidate 44:** `c0*sin(c1+t) + c2 + c3*x + c4*x**3 + c5*x**5 + c6*v`. Set c2=c3=c4=c5=0: `c0*sin(c1+t) + c6*v`. Missing v**3 and v*exp(-|v|). **NO MATCH**
